<p><b>Cologne</b> (<span class="nowrap"><small>English:</small> <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Köln</span>, <small>pronounced</small> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">[kœln]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Koeln.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/18/Koeln.ogg" class="internal" title="Koeln.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>, <a href="/wiki/Colognian_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Colognian language">Colognian</a>: <span lang="ksh" xml:lang="ksh"><i>Kölle</i></span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Colognian" title="Help:IPA/Colognian">[ˈkœɫə]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Koelle.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e2/Koelle.ogg" class="internal" title="Koelle.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>) is the largest city in the German <a href="/wiki/Federal_states_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal states of Germany">federal State</a> of <a href="/wiki/North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="North Rhine-Westphalia">North Rhine-Westphalia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Germany_by_population" title="List of cities in Germany by population">fourth populated city</a> in <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> (after <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>). It is located within the <a href="/wiki/Rhine-Ruhr" title="Rhine-Ruhr">Rhine-Ruhr</a> metropolitan region which is <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_regions_in_Germany#Metropolitan_regions" title="Metropolitan regions in Germany">Germany's largest</a> and one of <a href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_Europe#Metropolitan_areas" title="List of metropolitan areas in Europe">Europe's major metropolitan areas</a>. Cologne is about 45 kilometres (28&#160;mi) southwest of North Rhine-Westphalia's capital of <a href="/wiki/Dusseldorf" class="mw-redirect" title="Dusseldorf">Dusseldorf</a> and 25 kilometres (16&#160;mi) northwest of <a href="/wiki/Bonn" title="Bonn">Bonn</a>.</p>
<p>Cologne is located on both sides of the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a>, near Germany's borders with <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>. The city's famous <a href="/wiki/Cologne_Cathedral" title="Cologne Cathedral">Cologne Cathedral</a> (<i>Kölner Dom</i>) is the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_bishops_and_archbishops_of_Cologne" class="mw-redirect" title="List of bishops and archbishops of Cologne">Archbishop of Cologne</a>. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cologne" title="University of Cologne">University of Cologne</a> (<i>Universität zu Köln</i>) is one of Europe's oldest and largest universities.<sup id="cite_ref-Cologneeconomy_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cologneeconomy-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cologne was founded and established in <a href="/wiki/Ubii" title="Ubii">Ubii</a> territory in the 1st century AD as the <a href="/wiki/Roman_colony" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman colony">Roman</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Colonia_Claudia_Ara_Agrippinensium" title="Colonia Claudia Ara Agrippinensium">Colonia Claudia Ara Agrippinensium</a></i>, the first word of which is the origin of its name.<sup id="cite_ref-Cologne_History_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cologne_History-3">[3]</a></sup> (An alternative Latin name of the settlement is <i>Augusta Ubiorum</i>, after the Ubii.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup>) "Cologne", the French version of the city's name, has become standard in English as well. The city functioned as the capital of the Roman province of <i><a href="/wiki/Germania_Inferior" title="Germania Inferior">Germania Inferior</a></i> and as the headquarters of the Roman military in the region until occupied by the <a href="/wiki/Ripuarian_Franks" title="Ripuarian Franks">Franks</a> in 462. During the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> it flourished on one of the most important major <a href="/wiki/Trade_routes" class="mw-redirect" title="Trade routes">trade routes</a> between east and west in Europe. Cologne was one of the leading members of the <a href="/wiki/Hanseatic_League" title="Hanseatic League">Hanseatic League</a> and one of the largest cities north of the <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a> in medieval and Renaissance times. Prior to <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> the city had undergone several occupations by the French and also by the British (1918–1926). Cologne was one of the most heavily bombed cities in Germany during World War II, with the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a> (RAF) dropping 34,711 long tons (35,268 tonnes) of <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Cologne_in_World_War_II" title="Bombing of Cologne in World War II">bombs on the city</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> The bombing reduced the population by 95%, mainly due to evacuation, and destroyed almost the entire city. With the intention of restoring as many historic buildings as possible, the successful postwar rebuilding has resulted in a very mixed and unique cityscape.</p>
<p>Cologne is a major cultural centre for the <a href="/wiki/Rhineland" title="Rhineland">Rhineland</a>; it hosts more than 30 museums and hundreds of galleries. Exhibitions range from local ancient Roman archeological sites to contemporary graphics and sculpture. The <a href="/wiki/Cologne_Trade_Fair" class="mw-redirect" title="Cologne Trade Fair">Cologne Trade Fair</a> hosts a number of <a href="/wiki/Trade_show" class="mw-redirect" title="Trade show">trade shows</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Art_Cologne" title="Art Cologne">Art Cologne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Imm_Cologne" title="Imm Cologne">imm Cologne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gamescom" title="Gamescom">Gamescom</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Photokina" title="Photokina">Photokina</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Cologne" title="History of Cologne">History of Cologne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Cologne" title="Timeline of Cologne">Timeline of Cologne</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_Cologne">Roman Cologne</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Roman Cologne">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wall_painting_with_Dionysian_scenes_from_a_luxurious_Roman_villa_excavated_to_the_south_of_the_cathedral,_Romisch-Germanisches_Museum,_Cologne_(8119154487).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Wall_painting_with_Dionysian_scenes_from_a_luxurious_Roman_villa_excavated_to_the_south_of_the_cathedral%2C_Romisch-Germanisches_Museum%2C_Cologne_%288119154487%29.jpg/220px-Wall_painting_with_Dionysian_scenes_from_a_luxurious_Roman_villa_excavated_to_the_south_of_the_cathedral%2C_Romisch-Germanisches_Museum%2C_Cologne_%288119154487%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Wall_painting_with_Dionysian_scenes_from_a_luxurious_Roman_villa_excavated_to_the_south_of_the_cathedral%2C_Romisch-Germanisches_Museum%2C_Cologne_%288119154487%29.jpg/330px-Wall_painting_with_Dionysian_scenes_from_a_luxurious_Roman_villa_excavated_to_the_south_of_the_cathedral%2C_Romisch-Germanisches_Museum%2C_Cologne_%288119154487%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Wall_painting_with_Dionysian_scenes_from_a_luxurious_Roman_villa_excavated_to_the_south_of_the_cathedral%2C_Romisch-Germanisches_Museum%2C_Cologne_%288119154487%29.jpg/440px-Wall_painting_with_Dionysian_scenes_from_a_luxurious_Roman_villa_excavated_to_the_south_of_the_cathedral%2C_Romisch-Germanisches_Museum%2C_Cologne_%288119154487%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4263" data-file-height="3199" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wall_painting_with_Dionysian_scenes_from_a_luxurious_Roman_villa_excavated_to_the_south_of_the_cathedral,_Romisch-Germanisches_Museum,_Cologne_(8119154487).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Fresco with <a href="/wiki/Dionysian_mysteries" class="mw-redirect" title="Dionysian mysteries">Dionysian scenes</a> from a Roman villa of Cologne, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> (site of the ancient city <a href="/wiki/Colonia_Claudia_Ara_Agrippinensium" title="Colonia Claudia Ara Agrippinensium">Colonia Claudia Ara Agrippinensium</a>), 3rd century AD, <a href="/wiki/Romano-Germanic_Museum" title="Romano-Germanic Museum">Romano-Germanic Museum</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first urban settlement on the grounds of modern-day Cologne was <i>Oppidum Ubiorum</i>, founded in 38&#160;BC by the <a href="/wiki/Ubii" title="Ubii">Ubii</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Germani_cisrhenani" title="Germani cisrhenani">Cisrhenian</a> <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic tribe</a>. In 50&#160;AD, the Romans founded Colonia on the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a><sup id="cite_ref-Cologne_History_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cologne_History-3">[3]</a></sup> and the city became the provincial capital of <a href="/wiki/Germania_Inferior" title="Germania Inferior">Germania Inferior</a> in 85&#160;AD.<sup id="cite_ref-Facts_and_figures_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Facts_and_figures-6">[6]</a></sup> The city was named <i><a href="/wiki/Colonia_Claudia_Ara_Agrippinensium" title="Colonia Claudia Ara Agrippinensium">Colonia Claudia Ara Agrippinensium</a></i> in 50&#160;AD.<sup id="cite_ref-Facts_and_figures_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Facts_and_figures-6">[6]</a></sup> Considerable Roman remains can be found in present-day Cologne, especially near the wharf area, where a notable discovery of a 1900-year-old Roman boat was made in late 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> From 260 to 271 Cologne was the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Gallic_Empire" title="Gallic Empire">Gallic Empire</a> under <a href="/wiki/Postumus" title="Postumus">Postumus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Aurelius_Marius" title="Marcus Aurelius Marius">Marius</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Victorinus" title="Victorinus">Victorinus</a>. In 310 under <a href="/wiki/Constantine_I_(emperor)" class="mw-redirect" title="Constantine I (emperor)">Constantine</a> a bridge was built over the Rhine at Cologne. Roman imperial governors resided in the city and it became one of the most important trade and production centres in the Roman Empire north of the Alps.<sup id="cite_ref-Cologne_History_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cologne_History-3">[3]</a></sup> Cologne is shown on the <a href="/wiki/4th_century" title="4th century">4th century</a> <a href="/wiki/Peutinger_Map" class="mw-redirect" title="Peutinger Map">Peutinger Map</a>.</p>
<p>Maternus, who was elected as bishop in 313, was the first known bishop of Cologne. The city was the capital of a Roman province until occupied by the <a href="/wiki/Ripuarian_Franks" title="Ripuarian Franks">Ripuarian Franks</a> in 462. Parts of the original Roman sewers are preserved underneath the city, with the <a href="/wiki/Cologne_sewerage_system" title="Cologne sewerage system">new sewerage system</a> having opened in 1890.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Early medieval Cologne was part of <a href="/wiki/Austrasia" title="Austrasia">Austrasia</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Frankish_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankish Empire">Frankish Empire</a>. Cologne had been the seat of a bishop since the Roman period; under <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a>, in 795, bishop <a href="/wiki/Hildebold" title="Hildebold">Hildebold</a> was promoted to <a href="/wiki/Archbishop" title="Archbishop">archbishop</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Cologne_History_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cologne_History-3">[3]</a></sup> In 843, Cologne became a city within the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Verdun" title="Treaty of Verdun">Treaty of Verdun</a>-created <a href="/wiki/East_Francia" title="East Francia">East Francia</a>.</p>
<p>In 953, the archbishops of Cologne first gained noteworthy secular power, when bishop <a href="/wiki/Bruno_I,_Archbishop_of_Cologne" class="mw-redirect" title="Bruno I, Archbishop of Cologne">Bruno</a> was appointed as duke by his brother <a href="/wiki/Otto_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Otto I, Holy Roman Emperor">Otto I</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Germany" title="Kingdom of Germany">King of Germany</a>. In order to weaken the secular nobility, who threatened his power, Otto endowed Bruno and his successors on the bishop's see with the prerogatives of secular princes, thus establishing the <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_Cologne" title="Electorate of Cologne">Electorate of Cologne</a>, formed by the temporal possessions of the archbishopric and included in the end a strip of territory along the left Bank of the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a> east of <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BClich" title="Jülich">Jülich</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Westphalia" title="Duchy of Westphalia">Duchy of Westphalia</a> on the other side of the Rhine, beyond <a href="/wiki/Berg_(state)" class="mw-redirect" title="Berg (state)">Berg</a> and <a href="/wiki/County_of_Mark" title="County of Mark">Mark</a>. By the end of the 12th century, the Archbishop of Cologne was one of the seven electors of the Holy Roman Emperor. Besides being prince elector, he was Arch-chancellor of Italy as well, technically from 1238 and permanently from 1263 until 1803.</p>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Worringen" title="Battle of Worringen">Battle of Worringen</a> in 1288, Cologne gained its independence from the archbishops and became a <a href="/wiki/Free_Imperial_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Free Imperial City">Free City</a>. Archbishop <a href="/wiki/Sigfried_II_von_Westerburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Sigfried II von Westerburg">Sigfried II von Westerburg</a> was forced into exile in <a href="/wiki/Bonn" title="Bonn">Bonn</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Catholic_Encyclopedia_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Catholic_Encyclopedia-8">[8]</a></sup> The archbishop nevertheless preserved the right of capital punishment. Thus the municipal council (though in strict political opposition towards the archbishop) depended upon him in all matters concerning criminal justice. This included torture, which sentence was only allowed to be handed down by the episcopal judge, the so-called "Greve". This legal situation lasted until the French conquest of Cologne.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Besides its economic and political significance Cologne also became an important centre of medieval pilgrimage, when Cologne's Archbishop <a href="/wiki/Rainald_of_Dassel" title="Rainald of Dassel">Rainald of Dassel</a> gave the relics of the <a href="/wiki/Three_Wise_Men" class="mw-redirect" title="Three Wise Men">Three Wise Men</a> to Cologne's cathedral in 1164 (after they in fact had been captured from <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>). Besides the three magi Cologne preserves the relics of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Ursula" title="Saint Ursula">Saint Ursula</a> and <a href="/wiki/Albertus_Magnus" title="Albertus Magnus">Albertus Magnus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cologne's location on the river Rhine placed it at the intersection of the major <a href="/wiki/Trade_route" title="Trade route">trade routes</a> between east and west as well as the main Western Europe trade route, South - North Northern Italy-Flanders. These two trade routes were the basis of Cologne's growth. By 1300 the city population was 50,000-55,000.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Cologne was a member of the <a href="/wiki/Hanseatic_League" title="Hanseatic League">Hanseatic League</a> in 1475, when <a href="/wiki/Frederick_III,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Frederick III, Holy Roman Emperor">Frederick III</a> confirmed the city's imperial immediacy.<sup id="cite_ref-Cologne_History_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cologne_History-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<div class="center">
<div class="thumb tnone">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:552px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cologn1411.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Cologn1411.jpg/550px-Cologn1411.jpg" width="550" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Cologn1411.jpg/825px-Cologn1411.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Cologn1411.jpg/1100px-Cologn1411.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2712" data-file-height="888" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cologn1411.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cologne around 1411</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_modern_history">Early modern history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Early modern history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The economic structures of medieval and early modern Cologne were characterised by the city's status as a major harbour and transport hub on the Rhine. Craftsmanship was organised by self-administering guilds, some of which were exclusive to women.</p>
<p>As a free city, Cologne was a sovereign state within the Holy Roman Empire and as such had the right (and obligation) to maintain its own military force. As they wore a red uniform, these troops were known as the <i>Rote Funken</i> (red sparks). These soldiers were part of the Army of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> ("Reichskontingent") and fought in the wars of the 17th and 18th century, including the wars against revolutionary France, when the small force was almost completely wiped out in combat. The tradition of these troops is preserved as a military persiflage by Cologne's most outstanding carnival society, the <i>Rote Funken</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>The free city of Cologne must not be confused with the <a href="/wiki/Archbishopric_of_Cologne" class="mw-redirect" title="Archbishopric of Cologne">Archbishopric of Cologne</a> which was a state of its own within the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>. Since the second half of the 16th century the archbishops were drawn from the <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavaria</a> <a href="/wiki/Wittelsbach" class="mw-redirect" title="Wittelsbach">Wittelsbach</a> dynasty. Due to the free status of Cologne, the archbishops were usually not allowed to enter the city. Thus they took up residence in <a href="/wiki/Bonn" title="Bonn">Bonn</a> and later in <a href="/wiki/Br%C3%BChl,_North_Rhine-Westphalia" class="mw-redirect" title="Brühl, North Rhine-Westphalia">Brühl</a> on the Rhine. As members of an influential and powerful family, and supported by their outstanding status as <a href="/wiki/Prince-elector" title="Prince-elector">electors</a>, the archbishops of Cologne repeatedly challenged and threatened the free status of Cologne during the 17th and 18th centuries, resulting in complicated affairs, which were handled by diplomatic means and propaganda as well as by the supreme courts of the Holy Roman Empire.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="From_the_19th_century_until_World_War_II">From the 19th century until World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: From the 19th century until World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hohestra%C3%9Fe_-_C%C3%B6ln_am_Rhein,_1912.tif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Hohestra%C3%9Fe_-_C%C3%B6ln_am_Rhein%2C_1912.tif/lossy-page1-220px-Hohestra%C3%9Fe_-_C%C3%B6ln_am_Rhein%2C_1912.tif.jpg" width="220" height="342" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Hohestra%C3%9Fe_-_C%C3%B6ln_am_Rhein%2C_1912.tif/lossy-page1-330px-Hohestra%C3%9Fe_-_C%C3%B6ln_am_Rhein%2C_1912.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Hohestra%C3%9Fe_-_C%C3%B6ln_am_Rhein%2C_1912.tif/lossy-page1-440px-Hohestra%C3%9Fe_-_C%C3%B6ln_am_Rhein%2C_1912.tif.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2088" data-file-height="3245" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hohestra%C3%9Fe_-_C%C3%B6ln_am_Rhein,_1912.tif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hohestraße, 1912</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:H%C3%A4ngebr%C3%BCcke_-_K%C3%B6ln_(1).tif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/H%C3%A4ngebr%C3%BCcke_-_K%C3%B6ln_%281%29.tif/lossy-page1-220px-H%C3%A4ngebr%C3%BCcke_-_K%C3%B6ln_%281%29.tif.jpg" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/H%C3%A4ngebr%C3%BCcke_-_K%C3%B6ln_%281%29.tif/lossy-page1-330px-H%C3%A4ngebr%C3%BCcke_-_K%C3%B6ln_%281%29.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/H%C3%A4ngebr%C3%BCcke_-_K%C3%B6ln_%281%29.tif/lossy-page1-440px-H%C3%A4ngebr%C3%BCcke_-_K%C3%B6ln_%281%29.tif.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3300" data-file-height="2149" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:H%C3%A4ngebr%C3%BCcke_-_K%C3%B6ln_(1).tif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hängebrücke</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cologne lost its status as a <a href="/wiki/Free_Imperial_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Free Imperial City">free city</a> during the French period. According to the Peace <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lun%C3%A9ville" title="Treaty of Lunéville">Treaty of Lunéville</a> (1801) all the territories of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> on the left bank of the Rhine were officially incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/French_First_Republic" title="French First Republic">French Republic</a> (which had already occupied Cologne in 1794). Thus this region later became part of <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_I_of_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleon I of France">Napoleon's</a> Empire. Cologne was part of the French <a href="/wiki/Department_(administrative_division)" class="mw-redirect" title="Department (administrative division)">Département</a> <a href="/wiki/Roer_(department)" title="Roer (department)">Roer</a> (named after the river Roer, German: <a href="/wiki/Rur" title="Rur">Rur</a>) with <a href="/wiki/Aachen" title="Aachen">Aachen</a> (French: Aix-la-Chapelle) as its capital. The French modernised public life, for example by introducing the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_code" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleonic code">Napoleonic code</a> and removing the old elites from power. The <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_code" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleonic code">Napoleonic code</a> remained in use on the left bank of the Rhine until 1900, when a unified civil code (the <i><a href="/wiki/B%C3%BCrgerliches_Gesetzbuch" title="Bürgerliches Gesetzbuch">Bürgerliches Gesetzbuch</a></i>) was introduced in the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a>. In 1815 at the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Congress of Vienna</a>, Cologne was made part of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Kingdom of Prussia</a>, first in the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_J%C3%BClich-Cleves-Berg" title="Province of Jülich-Cleves-Berg">Jülich-Cleves-Berg province</a> and then the <a href="/wiki/Rhine_province" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhine province">Rhine province</a>.</p>
<p>The permanent tensions between the Roman Catholic <a href="/wiki/Rhineland" title="Rhineland">Rhineland</a> and the overwhelmingly Protestant Prussian state repeatedly escalated with Cologne being in the focus of the conflict. In 1837 the archbishop of Cologne, <a href="/wiki/Clemens_August_von_Droste-Vischering" title="Clemens August von Droste-Vischering">Clemens August von Droste-Vischering</a>, was arrested and imprisoned for two years after a dispute over the legal status of marriages between Protestants and Roman Catholics (<i>Mischehenstreit</i>). In 1874, during the <a href="/wiki/Kulturkampf" title="Kulturkampf">Kulturkampf</a>, Archbishop <a href="/wiki/Paul_Melchers" title="Paul Melchers">Paul Melchers</a> was imprisoned before taking refuge in the Netherlands. These conflicts alienated the Catholic population from Berlin and contributed to a deeply felt anti-Prussian resentment, which was still significant after World War II, when the former mayor of Cologne, <a href="/wiki/Konrad_Adenauer" title="Konrad Adenauer">Konrad Adenauer</a>, became the first West German chancellor.</p>
<p>During the 19th and 20th centuries, Cologne absorbed numerous surrounding towns, and by World War&#160;I had already grown to 700,000 inhabitants. Industrialisation changed the city and spurred its growth. Vehicle and engine manufacturing were especially successful, though heavy industry was less ubiquitous than in the <a href="/wiki/Ruhr_area" class="mw-redirect" title="Ruhr area">Ruhr area</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Cologne_Cathedral" title="Cologne Cathedral">cathedral</a>, started in 1248 but abandoned around 1560, was eventually finished in 1880 not just as a place of worship but also as a German national monument celebrating the newly founded <a href="/wiki/German_empire" class="mw-redirect" title="German empire">German empire</a> and the continuity of the German nation since the Middle Ages. Some of this urban growth occurred at the expense of the city's historic heritage with much being demolished (for example, the city walls or the area around the cathedral) and sometimes replaced by contemporary buildings.</p>
<p>Cologne was designated as one of the <a href="/wiki/Fortresses_of_the_German_Confederation" title="Fortresses of the German Confederation">Fortresses of the German Confederation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-USM_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USM-12">[12]</a></sup> It was turned into a heavily armed fortress (opposing the French and Belgian fortresses of <a href="/wiki/Verdun" title="Verdun">Verdun</a> and <a href="/wiki/Li%C3%A8ge_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Liège (city)">Liège</a>) with two fortified belts surrounding the city, the remains of which can be seen to this day.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> The military demands on what became Germany's largest fortress presented a significant obstacle to urban development, with forts, bunkers, and wide defensive dugouts completely encircling the city and preventing expansion; this resulted in a very densely built-up area within the city itself.</p>
<p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War&#160;I</a> Cologne was the target of several minor air raids, but suffered no significant damage. Cologne was occupied by the <a href="/wiki/British_Army_of_the_Rhine" title="British Army of the Rhine">British Army of the Rhine</a> until 1926, under the terms of the Armistice and the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Peace_Treaty_of_Versailles" class="mw-redirect" title="Peace Treaty of Versailles">Versailles Peace Treaty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> In contrast with the harsh behaviour of the French occupation troops in Germany, the British forces were more lenient to the local population. <a href="/wiki/Konrad_Adenauer" title="Konrad Adenauer">Konrad Adenauer</a>, the mayor of Cologne from 1917 until 1933 and later a West German chancellor, acknowledged the political impact of this approach, especially since Britain had opposed French demands for a permanent Allied occupation of the entire Rhineland.</p>
<p>As part of the demilitarisation of the <a href="/wiki/Rhineland" title="Rhineland">Rhineland</a>, the city's fortifications had to be dismantled. This was an opportunity to create two green belts (<i>Grüngürtel</i>) around the city by converting the fortifications and their fields of fire into large public parks. This was not completed until 1933. In 1919 the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cologne" title="University of Cologne">University of Cologne</a>, closed by the French in 1798, was reopened. This was considered to be a replacement for the loss of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Strasbourg" title="University of Strasbourg">University of Strasbourg</a> on the west bank of the Rhine, which reverted to France with the rest of <a href="/wiki/Alsace" title="Alsace">Alsace</a>. Cologne prospered during the <a href="/wiki/Weimar_Republic" title="Weimar Republic">Weimar Republic</a> (1919–33), and progress was made especially in public governance, city planning, housing and social affairs. Social housing projects were considered exemplary and were copied by other German cities. Cologne competed to host the Olympics, and a modern sports stadium was erected at Müngersdorf. When the British occupation ended, the prohibition of civil aviation was lifted and <a href="/wiki/Cologne_Butzweilerhof_Airport" title="Cologne Butzweilerhof Airport">Cologne Butzweilerhof Airport</a> soon became a hub for national and international air traffic, second in Germany only to <a href="/wiki/Tempelhof_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Tempelhof International Airport">Berlin Tempelhof Airport</a>.</p>
<p>The democratic parties lost the local elections in Cologne in March 1933 to the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">Nazi Party</a> and other right wing parties. The Nazis then arrested the <a href="/wiki/KPD" class="mw-redirect" title="KPD">Communist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="Social Democratic Party of Germany">Social Democrats</a> members of the city assembly, and Mayor Adenauer was dismissed. Compared to some other major cities, however, the Nazis never gained decisive support in Cologne. (Significantly, the number of votes cast for the Nazi Party in <a href="/wiki/Reichstag_(Weimar_Republic)" title="Reichstag (Weimar Republic)">Reichstag</a> elections had always been the national average.)<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> By 1939 the population had risen to 772,221 inhabitants.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II">World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Koeln_1945.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Koeln_1945.jpg/220px-Koeln_1945.jpg" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Koeln_1945.jpg/330px-Koeln_1945.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Koeln_1945.jpg/440px-Koeln_1945.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2919" data-file-height="2092" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Koeln_1945.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The devastation of Cologne, 1945</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During World War II, Cologne was a Military Area Command Headquarters (<i>Militärbereichshauptkommandoquartier</i>) for the <a href="/wiki/Military_district_(Germany)" title="Military district (Germany)">Military District</a> (<i>Wehrkreis</i>) VI of <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnster" title="Münster">Münster</a>. Cologne was under the command of Lieutenant-General Freiherr Roeder von Diersburg, who was responsible for military operations in <a href="/wiki/Bonn" title="Bonn">Bonn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siegburg" title="Siegburg">Siegburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aachen" title="Aachen">Aachen</a>, <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BClich" title="Jülich">Jülich</a>, <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCren" title="Düren">Düren</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Monschau" title="Monschau">Monschau</a>. Cologne was home to the 211th Infantry Regiment and the 26th Artillery Regiment.</p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Cologne_in_World_War_II" title="Bombing of Cologne in World War II">Bombing of Cologne in World War II</a>, Cologne endured 262 air raids<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> by the Western <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allies</a>, which caused approximately 20,000 civilian casualties and almost completely wiped out the central part of the city. During the night of 31 May 1942, Cologne was the target of "<a href="/wiki/Operation_Millennium" class="mw-redirect" title="Operation Millennium">Operation Millennium</a>", the first 1,000 bomber raid by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a> in World War&#160;II. 1,046 heavy bombers attacked their target with 1,455 tons of explosives, approximately two-thirds of which were incendiary.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> This raid lasted about 75 minutes, destroyed 600 acres (243&#160;ha) of built-up area, killed 486 civilians and made 59,000 people homeless.</p>
<p>Cologne was taken by the American <a href="/wiki/First_United_States_Army#World_War_II" title="First United States Army">First Army</a> in early March, 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> By the end of the war, the population of Cologne had been reduced by 95 per cent. This loss was mainly caused by a massive evacuation of the people to more rural areas. The same happened in many other German cities in the last two years of war. By the end of 1945, however, the population had already recovered to approximately 500,000.</p>
<p>By the end of the war, essentially all of Cologne's pre-war <a href="/wiki/Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> population of 11,000 had been deported or killed by the Nazis.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> The six synagogues of the city were destroyed. The <a href="/wiki/Roonstrasse_Synagogue" title="Roonstrasse Synagogue">synagogue on Roonstraße</a> was rebuilt in 1959.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-war_Cologne_until_today">Post-war Cologne until today</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Post-war Cologne until today">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;"><a href="/wiki/File:K%C3%B6lnFromTheISS.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/K%C3%B6lnFromTheISS.jpg/275px-K%C3%B6lnFromTheISS.jpg" width="275" height="415" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/K%C3%B6lnFromTheISS.jpg/413px-K%C3%B6lnFromTheISS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/K%C3%B6lnFromTheISS.jpg/550px-K%C3%B6lnFromTheISS.jpg 2x" data-file-width="679" data-file-height="1024" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:K%C3%B6lnFromTheISS.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cologne, seen from the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Despite Cologne's status as the largest city in the region, nearby <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Düsseldorf">Düsseldorf</a> was chosen as the political capital of the <a href="/wiki/States_of_Germany" title="States of Germany">federated state</a> of <a href="/wiki/North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="North Rhine-Westphalia">North Rhine-Westphalia</a>. With <a href="/wiki/Bonn" title="Bonn">Bonn</a> being chosen as the provisional federal capital (<i>provisorische Bundeshauptstadt</i>) and seat of the government of the Federal Republic of Germany (then informally <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a>), Cologne benefited by being sandwiched between two important political centres. The city became–and still is–home to a number of federal agencies and organizations. After reunification in 1990, Berlin was made the capital of Germany.</p>
<p>In 1945 architect and urban planner <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Schwarz_(architect)" title="Rudolf Schwarz (architect)">Rudolf Schwarz</a> called Cologne the "world's greatest heap of rubble". Schwarz designed the master plan for reconstruction in 1947, which included the construction of several new thoroughfares through the city centre, especially the <i>Nord-Süd-Fahrt</i> ("North-South-Drive"). The master plan took into consideration the fact that even shortly after the war a large increase in automobile traffic could be anticipated. Plans for new roads had already, to a certain degree, evolved under the Nazi administration, but the actual construction became easier when most of the city centre was in ruins.</p>
<p>The destruction of 95% of the city centre, including the famous <a href="/wiki/Twelve_Romanesque_churches_of_Cologne" title="Twelve Romanesque churches of Cologne">Twelve Romanesque churches</a> such as <a href="/wiki/St._Gereon%27s_Basilica" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Gereon's Basilica">St.&#160;Gereon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Great_St._Martin_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Great St. Martin Church">Great St.&#160;Martin</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Maria_im_Kapitol" title="St. Maria im Kapitol">St.&#160;Maria im Kapitol</a> and several other monuments in World War&#160;II, meant a tremendous loss of cultural treasures. The rebuilding of those churches and other landmarks such as the Gürzenich event hall was not undisputed among leading architects and art historians at that time, but in most cases, civil intention prevailed. The reconstruction lasted until the 1990s, when the Romanesque church of <a href="/wiki/St._Kunibert_(Cologne)" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Kunibert (Cologne)">St.&#160;Kunibert</a> was finished.</p>
<p>In 1959, the city's population reached pre-war numbers again. It then grew steadily, exceeding 1&#160;million for about one year from 1975. It remained just below that until mid-2010, when it exceeded 1&#160;million again.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2013-08-10_07-18-55_Ballonfahrt_%C3%BCber_K%C3%B6ln_EH_0626.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/2013-08-10_07-18-55_Ballonfahrt_%C3%BCber_K%C3%B6ln_EH_0626.jpg/220px-2013-08-10_07-18-55_Ballonfahrt_%C3%BCber_K%C3%B6ln_EH_0626.jpg" width="220" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/2013-08-10_07-18-55_Ballonfahrt_%C3%BCber_K%C3%B6ln_EH_0626.jpg/330px-2013-08-10_07-18-55_Ballonfahrt_%C3%BCber_K%C3%B6ln_EH_0626.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/2013-08-10_07-18-55_Ballonfahrt_%C3%BCber_K%C3%B6ln_EH_0626.jpg/440px-2013-08-10_07-18-55_Ballonfahrt_%C3%BCber_K%C3%B6ln_EH_0626.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5352" data-file-height="2923" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

Cologne in 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-reunification">Post-reunification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Post-reunification">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1983_09_15_to_23_Envelope_of_the_Letter_from_Odessa_to_Cuba.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/1983_09_15_to_23_Envelope_of_the_Letter_from_Odessa_to_Cuba.jpg/220px-1983_09_15_to_23_Envelope_of_the_Letter_from_Odessa_to_Cuba.jpg" width="220" height="239" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/1983_09_15_to_23_Envelope_of_the_Letter_from_Odessa_to_Cuba.jpg/330px-1983_09_15_to_23_Envelope_of_the_Letter_from_Odessa_to_Cuba.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/1983_09_15_to_23_Envelope_of_the_Letter_from_Odessa_to_Cuba.jpg/440px-1983_09_15_to_23_Envelope_of_the_Letter_from_Odessa_to_Cuba.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2202" data-file-height="2388" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1983_09_15_to_23_Envelope_of_the_Letter_from_Odessa_to_Cuba.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Soviet letter's envelope in honor of the Internationale Philatelic Exhibition <i>LUPOSTA</i> in Cologne in 1983.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the 1980s and 1990s Cologne's economy prospered for two main reasons. The first was the growth in the number of media companies, both in the private and public sectors; they are especially catered for in the newly developed Media Park, which creates a strongly visual focal point in Cologne city centre and includes the <i>KölnTurm</i>, one of Cologne's most prominent high-rise buildings. The second was the permanent improvement of the diverse traffic infrastructure, which made Cologne one of the most easily accessible metropolitan areas in Central Europe.</p>
<p>Due to the economic success of the <a href="/wiki/Cologne_Trade_Fair" class="mw-redirect" title="Cologne Trade Fair">Cologne Trade Fair</a>, the city arranged a large extension to the fair site in 2005. At the same time the original buildings, which date back to the 1920s, were rented out to <a href="/wiki/RTL_Group" title="RTL Group">RTL</a>, Germany's largest private broadcaster, as their new corporate headquarters.</p>
<p>Cologne was the focus of the 2015 <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Eve_sexual_assaults_in_Germany" title="New Year's Eve sexual assaults in Germany">New Year's Eve sexual assaults</a>, with over 500 women reporting that they were sexually assaulted by persons of African and Arab appearance.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-waz2_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-waz2-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The metropolitan area encompasses over 405 square kilometres (156 square miles), extending around a central point that lies at 50° 56' 33 latitude and 6° 57' 32 longitude. The city's highest point is 118&#160;m (387.1&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Monte_Troodel%C3%B6h" title="Monte Troodelöh">Monte Troodelöh</a>) and its lowest point is 37.5&#160;m (123.0&#160;ft) above sea level (the <a href="/wiki/Worringer_Bruch" title="Worringer Bruch">Worringer Bruch</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> The city of Cologne lies within the larger area of the <a href="/wiki/Cologne_Lowland" title="Cologne Lowland">Cologne Lowland</a>, a cone-shaped area of southeastern Westphalia that lies between <a href="/wiki/Bonn" title="Bonn">Bonn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aachen" title="Aachen">Aachen</a> and <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Düsseldorf">Düsseldorf</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Districts">Districts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Districts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Cologne" title="Districts of Cologne">Districts of Cologne</a></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cologne is one of the warmest cities in Germany. It has a <a href="/wiki/Temperateness" class="mw-redirect" title="Temperateness">temperate</a>–<a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a> with cool winters and warm summers. It is also one of the cloudiest cities in Germany, with just 1568 hours of sun a year. Its average annual temperature is 10.3&#160;°C (51&#160;°F): 14.8&#160;°C (59&#160;°F) during the day and 5.8&#160;°C (42&#160;°F) at night. In January, the mean temperature is 2.6&#160;°C (37&#160;°F), while the mean temperature in July is 18.8&#160;°C (66&#160;°F). Temperatures can vary significantly over the course of a month with warmer and colder weather. Precipitation is spread evenly throughout the year with a light peak in summer due to showers and thunderstorms.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flood_protection">Flood protection</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Flood protection">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hochwasserschutz_in_K%C3%B6ln_(27774115055).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Hochwasserschutz_in_K%C3%B6ln_%2827774115055%29.jpg/220px-Hochwasserschutz_in_K%C3%B6ln_%2827774115055%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Hochwasserschutz_in_K%C3%B6ln_%2827774115055%29.jpg/330px-Hochwasserschutz_in_K%C3%B6ln_%2827774115055%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Hochwasserschutz_in_K%C3%B6ln_%2827774115055%29.jpg/440px-Hochwasserschutz_in_K%C3%B6ln_%2827774115055%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5472" data-file-height="3648" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hochwasserschutz_in_K%C3%B6ln_(27774115055).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Flood protection in Cologne</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10776,_K%C3%B6ln,_Hochwasser.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10776%2C_K%C3%B6ln%2C_Hochwasser.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10776%2C_K%C3%B6ln%2C_Hochwasser.jpg" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10776%2C_K%C3%B6ln%2C_Hochwasser.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10776%2C_K%C3%B6ln%2C_Hochwasser.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10776%2C_K%C3%B6ln%2C_Hochwasser.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10776%2C_K%C3%B6ln%2C_Hochwasser.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="553" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10776,_K%C3%B6ln,_Hochwasser.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The 1930 flood in Cologne</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cologne is regularly affected by <a href="/wiki/Flooding" class="mw-redirect" title="Flooding">flooding</a> from the Rhine and is considered the most flood-prone European city.<sup id="cite_ref-MITCH_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MITCH-28">[28]</a></sup> A city agency (<i>Stadtentwässerungsbetriebe Köln</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> "Cologne Urban Drainage Operations") manages an extensive flood control system which includes both permanent and mobile <a href="/wiki/Flood_wall" title="Flood wall">flood walls</a>, protection from rising waters for buildings close to the river banks, monitoring and forecasting systems, pumping stations and programmes to create or protect <a href="/wiki/Floodplain" title="Floodplain">floodplains</a>, and river embankments.<sup id="cite_ref-MITCH_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MITCH-28">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> The system was redesigned after a 1993 flood, which resulted in heavy damage.<sup id="cite_ref-MITCH_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MITCH-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1235" data-file-height="650" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">USA</a></td>
<td>3,567</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In the Roman Empire the city was large and rich with a population of 40,000 in 100–200&#160;AD.<sup id="cite_ref-google_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-google-32">[32]</a></sup> The city was home to around 20,000 people in 1000&#160;AD, growing to 50,000 in 1200&#160;AD. The <a href="/wiki/Rhineland" title="Rhineland">Rhineland</a> metropolis still had 50,000 residents in 1300&#160;AD.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.dk_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.dk-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-harvard_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-harvard-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cologne is the fourth-largest city in Germany after <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>. As of 31 December 2016, there were 1,080,701 people registered as living in Cologne in an area of 401.15&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (154.88&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population density</a> was 2,641/km<sup>2</sup> (6,840/sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> The metropolitan area of the <a href="/wiki/Cologne_Bonn_Region" title="Cologne Bonn Region">Cologne Bonn Region</a> is home to 3,573,500 living on 4,415/km<sup>2</sup> (11,430/sq&#160;mi). <sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> It is part of the polycentric megacity region <a href="/wiki/Rhine-Ruhr" title="Rhine-Ruhr">Rhine-Ruhr</a> with a population of over 11,000,000 people.</p>
<p>There were 546,498 women and 522,694 men in Cologne. For every 1,000 males, there were 1,046 females. In 2015, there were 11,337 births in Cologne (of which 34.53% were to unmarried women); 7,704 marriages and 2,203 divorces, and 9,629 deaths. In the city, the population was spread out with 15.6% under the age of 18, and 17.6% were 65 years of age or older. 163 people in Cologne were over the age of 100. <sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the Statistical Office of the City of Cologne, the number of people with a migrant background is at 36.7% (393,7936). 2,537 people acquired German citizenship in 2015. <sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, there were 557,090 households, of which 18.3% had children under the age of 18; 50.6% of all households were made up of singles. 8.7% of all households were single parent households. The average household size was 1.87. <sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Colognian_dialect" title="Colognian dialect">Colognian dialect</a></div>
<p><b>Colognian</b> or <b>Kölsch</b> (<small>Colognian (Kölsch) pronunciation:</small> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Colognian" title="Help:IPA/Colognian">[kœɫːʃ]</a></span>) (natively <i>Kölsch Platt</i>) is a small set of very closely related dialects, or variants, of the <a href="/wiki/Ripuarian_language" title="Ripuarian language">Ripuarian</a> <a href="/wiki/Central_German" title="Central German">Central German</a> group of languages. These dialects are spoken in the area covered by the Archdiocese and former <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_Cologne" title="Electorate of Cologne">Electorate of Cologne</a> reaching from <a href="/wiki/Neuss" title="Neuss">Neuss</a> in the north to just south of <a href="/wiki/Bonn" title="Bonn">Bonn</a>, west to <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCren" title="Düren">Düren</a> and east to <a href="/wiki/Olpe,_Germany" title="Olpe, Germany">Olpe</a> in the North-West of <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>. Kölsch is one of the very few city dialects in Germany, besides for example, the <a href="/wiki/Berlinerisch_dialect" title="Berlinerisch dialect">dialect</a> spoken in <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Slightly more than half of the residents of Cologne are members of a religion. As of 2015, 35.5% of the population belonged to the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a>, the largest religious body, and 15.5% to the Evangelical Church. <sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Cologne is seat of seat of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Cologne" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Cologne">Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Cologne</a>. There are several mosques, including the <a href="/wiki/Turkish-Islamic_Union_for_Religious_Affairs" title="Turkish-Islamic Union for Religious Affairs">Turkish-Islamic Union for Religious Affairs</a> run <a href="/wiki/Cologne_Central_Mosque" title="Cologne Central Mosque">Cologne Central Mosque</a>. Cologne also has one of the oldest and largest Jewish communities in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Cologne_City_Hall" title="Cologne City Hall">Cologne City Hall</a></div>
<p>The city's administration is headed by the <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Cologne" title="List of mayors of Cologne">mayor</a> and the three deputy mayors.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_traditions_and_developments">Political traditions and developments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Political traditions and developments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The long tradition of a free imperial city, which long dominated an exclusively Catholic population and the age-old conflict between the church and the bourgeoisie (and within it between the patricians and craftsmen) has created its own political climate in Cologne. Various interest groups often form networks beyond party boundaries. The resulting web of relationships, with political, economic, and cultural links with each other in a system of mutual favours, obligations and dependencies, is called the 'Cologne coterie'. This has often led to an unusual proportional distribution in the city government and degenerated at times into corruption: in 1999, a "waste scandal" over kickbacks and illegal campaign contributions came to light, which led not only to the imprisonment of the entrepreneur Hellmut Trienekens, but also to the downfall of almost the entire leadership of the ruling Social Democrats.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mayor">Mayor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Mayor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Lord Mayor of Cologne is <a href="/wiki/Henriette_Reker" title="Henriette Reker">Henriette Reker</a>. She received 52.66% of the vote at the municipal election on 17 October 2015 and was appointed on 15 December 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Elections">Elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>City Councillors are elected for a five-year term and the Mayor has a six-year term.<sup id="cite_ref-Election_1_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Election_1-45">[45]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cityscape">Cityscape</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Cityscape">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:1008px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">

<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:1008px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cologne_-_Panoramic_Image_of_the_old_town_at_dusk.jpg" class="image" title="Panoramic view of the city at night as seen from Deutz; from left to right: Deutz Bridge, Great St.&#160;Martin Church, Cologne Cathedral, Hohenzollern Bridge"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Cologne_-_Panoramic_Image_of_the_old_town_at_dusk.jpg/1000px-Cologne_-_Panoramic_Image_of_the_old_town_at_dusk.jpg" width="1000" height="143" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Cologne_-_Panoramic_Image_of_the_old_town_at_dusk.jpg/1500px-Cologne_-_Panoramic_Image_of_the_old_town_at_dusk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Cologne_-_Panoramic_Image_of_the_old_town_at_dusk.jpg/2000px-Cologne_-_Panoramic_Image_of_the_old_town_at_dusk.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7000" data-file-height="1000" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cologne_-_Panoramic_Image_of_the_old_town_at_dusk.jpg" title="File:Cologne - Panoramic Image of the old town at dusk.jpg"></a></div>
Panoramic view of the city at night as seen from <a href="/wiki/Deutz,_Cologne" title="Deutz, Cologne">Deutz</a>; from left to right: Deutz Bridge, <a href="/wiki/Great_St._Martin_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Great St. Martin Church">Great St.&#160;Martin Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cologne_Cathedral" title="Cologne Cathedral">Cologne Cathedral</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hohenzollern_Bridge" title="Hohenzollern Bridge">Hohenzollern Bridge</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The inner city of Cologne was completely destroyed during World War&#160;II. The reconstruction of the city followed the style of the 1950s, while respecting the old layout and naming of the streets. Thus, the city today is characterized by simple and modest post-war buildings, with a few interspersed pre-war buildings which were reconstructed due to their historical importance. Some buildings of the "Wiederaufbauzeit" (era of reconstruction), for example the opera house by <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Riphahn" title="Wilhelm Riphahn">Wilhelm Riphahn</a>, are nowadays regarded as classics of modern architecture.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Nevertheless, the uncompromising style of the <a href="/wiki/Cologne_Opera" title="Cologne Opera">Cologne Opera</a> house and other modern buildings has remained controversial.</p>
<p>Green areas account for over a quarter of Cologne, which is approximately 75&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (807.29&#160;sq&#160;ft) of public green space for every inhabitant.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The presence of animals in Cologne is generally limited to insects, small rodents, and several species of birds. <a href="/wiki/Pigeon" class="mw-redirect" title="Pigeon">Pigeons</a> are the most often seen animals in Cologne, although the number of birds is augmented each year by a growing population of <a href="/wiki/Feral_organism" class="mw-redirect" title="Feral organism">feral</a> exotics, most visibly <a href="/wiki/Parrots" class="mw-redirect" title="Parrots">parrots</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Rose-ringed_parakeet" title="Rose-ringed parakeet">rose-ringed parakeet</a>. The sheltered climate in southeast <a href="/wiki/Northrhine-Westphalia" class="mw-redirect" title="Northrhine-Westphalia">Northrhine-Westphalia</a> allows these birds to survive through the winter, and in some cases they are displacing native species. The plumage of Cologne's green <a href="/wiki/Parrots" class="mw-redirect" title="Parrots">parrots</a> is highly visible even from a distance, and contrasts starkly with the otherwise muted colours of the cityscape.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Cologne had 5.8&#160;million overnight stays booked and 3.35&#160;million arrivals in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> The city also has the most pubs per capita in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-Nightlife_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nightlife-50">[50]</a></sup> The city has 70 clubs, "countless" bars, restaurants, and pubs.<sup id="cite_ref-Nightlife_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nightlife-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Landmarks">Landmarks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Landmarks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Churches">Churches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Churches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cologne_Cathedral" title="Cologne Cathedral">Cologne Cathedral</a> (German: <i>Kölner Dom</i>) is the city's most famous monument and the Cologne residents' most loved landmark. It is a <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic</a> church, started in 1248, and completed in 1880. In 1996, it was designated a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_site" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage site">World Heritage site</a>; it houses the <a href="/wiki/Shrine_of_the_Three_Kings" title="Shrine of the Three Kings">Shrine of the Three Kings</a>, which supposedly contains the <a href="/wiki/Relic" title="Relic">relics</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Biblical_Magi" title="Biblical Magi">Three Magi</a> (see also<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup>). Residents of Cologne sometimes refer to the cathedral as "the eternal construction site" (<i>die ewige Baustelle</i>).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Twelve_Romanesque_churches_of_Cologne" title="Twelve Romanesque churches of Cologne">Twelve Romanesque churches</a>: These buildings are outstanding examples of medieval church architecture. The origins of some of the churches go back as far as Roman times, for example St.&#160;Gereon, which was originally a chapel in a Roman graveyard. With the exception of St. Maria Lyskirchen all of these churches were very badly damaged during World War&#160;II. Reconstruction was only finished in the 1990s.</li>
</ul>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval_houses">Medieval houses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Medieval houses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Cologne City Hall (<i>Kölner Rathaus</i>), founded in the 12th century, is the oldest <a href="/wiki/City_hall" class="mw-redirect" title="City hall">city hall</a> in Germany still in use.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> The Renaissance style loggia and tower were added in the 15th century. Other famous buildings include the Gürzenich, Haus Saaleck and the Overstolzenhaus.</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval_city_gates">Medieval city gates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Medieval city gates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A_Plan_of_the_City_of_Cologne,_1800,_John_Stockdale-9832.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/A_Plan_of_the_City_of_Cologne%2C_1800%2C_John_Stockdale-9832.jpg/220px-A_Plan_of_the_City_of_Cologne%2C_1800%2C_John_Stockdale-9832.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/A_Plan_of_the_City_of_Cologne%2C_1800%2C_John_Stockdale-9832.jpg/330px-A_Plan_of_the_City_of_Cologne%2C_1800%2C_John_Stockdale-9832.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/A_Plan_of_the_City_of_Cologne%2C_1800%2C_John_Stockdale-9832.jpg/440px-A_Plan_of_the_City_of_Cologne%2C_1800%2C_John_Stockdale-9832.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3753" data-file-height="2815" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A_Plan_of_the_City_of_Cologne,_1800,_John_Stockdale-9832.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A plan published in 1800 shows the mediaeval city wall still intact, locating 16 gates (Nr. 36-51 in the legend), e.g. 47:&#160;Eigelsteintor, 43:&#160;Hahnentor, 39:&#160;Severinstor</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Of the once 12 medieval <a href="/wiki/City_gate" title="City gate">city gates</a>, only the Eigelsteintorburg at Ebertplatz, the Hahnentor at Rudolfplatz and the Severinstorburg at Chlodwigplatz still stand today.</p>

<p><br /></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Streets">Streets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Streets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Streets_in_Cologne" class="mw-redirect" title="Streets in Cologne">Streets in Cologne</a></div>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Cologne_Ring" title="Cologne Ring">Cologne Ring</a> boulevards (such as <i>Hohenzollernring</i>, <i>Kaiser-Wilhelm-Ring</i>, <i>Hansaring</i>) with their medieval city gates (such as <i>Hahnentorburg</i> on <i>Rudolfplatz</i>) are also known for their night life.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hohe_Stra%C3%9Fe" title="Hohe Straße">Hohe Straße</a> (literally: <i>High Street</i>) is one of the main shopping areas and extends past the cathedral in an approximately southerly direction. The street contains many gift shops, clothing stores, fast food restaurants and electronic goods dealers.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Schildergasse" title="Schildergasse">Schildergasse</a> – connects <i>Neumarkt</i> square at its western end to the <i>Hohe Strasse</i> shopping street at its eastern end and has been named the busiest shopping street in Europe with 13,000 people passing through every hour, according to a 2008 study by <a href="/wiki/GfK" title="GfK">GfK</a>.</li>
<li>Ehrenstraße – the shopping area around <i>Apostelnstrasse</i>, <i>Ehrenstrasse</i>, and <i>Rudolfplatz</i> is a little more on the quirky and stylish side.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bridges">Bridges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Bridges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Several bridges cross the Rhine in Cologne. They are (from South to North): the <a href="/wiki/Cologne_Rodenkirchen_Bridge" title="Cologne Rodenkirchen Bridge">Cologne Rodenkirchen Bridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Bridge_(Cologne)" title="South Bridge (Cologne)">South Bridge</a> (railway), Severin Bridge, Deutz Bridge, <a href="/wiki/Hohenzollern_Bridge" title="Hohenzollern Bridge">Hohenzollern Bridge</a> (railway), Zoo Bridge (<i>Zoobrücke</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Cologne_M%C3%BClheim_Bridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Cologne Mülheim Bridge">Cologne Mülheim Bridge</a>. In particular the iron <a href="/wiki/Tied_arch_bridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Tied arch bridge">tied arch</a> Hohenzollern Bridge (<i>Hohenzollernbrücke</i>) is a dominant landmark along the river embankment. A Rhine crossing of a special kind is provided by the <a href="/wiki/Cologne_Cable_Car" title="Cologne Cable Car">Cologne Cable Car</a> (German: <i>Kölner Seilbahn</i>), a cableway that runs across the Rhine between the <a href="/wiki/Cologne_Zoological_Garden" title="Cologne Zoological Garden">Cologne Zoological Garden</a> in Riehl and the <a href="/wiki/Rheinpark" title="Rheinpark">Rheinpark</a> in Deutz.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="High-rise_structures">High-rise structures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: High-rise structures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cologne's tallest structure is the <a href="/wiki/Colonius" title="Colonius">Colonius</a> telecommunication tower at 266&#160;m or 873&#160;ft. The observation deck has been closed since 1992. A selection of the tallest buildings in Cologne is listed below. Other tall structures include the Hansahochhaus (designed by architect Jacob Koerfer and completed in 1925—it was at one time Europe's tallest office building), the Kranhaus buildings at <a href="/wiki/Rheinauhafen" title="Rheinauhafen">Rheinauhafen</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Messeturm_K%C3%B6ln" title="Messeturm Köln">Messeturm Köln</a> ("trade fair tower").</p>
<table class="wikitable sortable" style="text-align:center; background:#fefef6; width:80%;">
<tr>
<th>Skyscraper</th>
<th class="unsortable">Image</th>
<th>Height in metres</th>
