<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kolumba_K%C3%B6ln_-_Innenhof.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Kolumba_K%C3%B6ln_-_Innenhof.jpg/220px-Kolumba_K%C3%B6ln_-_Innenhof.jpg" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Kolumba_K%C3%B6ln_-_Innenhof.jpg/330px-Kolumba_K%C3%B6ln_-_Innenhof.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Kolumba_K%C3%B6ln_-_Innenhof.jpg/440px-Kolumba_K%C3%B6ln_-_Innenhof.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3100" data-file-height="1900" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kolumba_K%C3%B6ln_-_Innenhof.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Courtyard of the <a href="/wiki/Kolumba" title="Kolumba">Kolumba</a> museum in 2007, designed by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Zumthor" title="Peter Zumthor">Peter Zumthor</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cologne has <a href="/wiki/List_of_museums_in_Cologne" title="List of museums in Cologne">several museums</a>. The famous <a href="/wiki/Roman-Germanic_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman-Germanic Museum">Roman-Germanic Museum</a> features art and architecture from the city's distant past; the <a href="/wiki/Museum_Ludwig" title="Museum Ludwig">Museum Ludwig</a> houses one of the most important collections of <a href="/wiki/Modern_art" title="Modern art">modern art</a> in Europe, including a <a href="/wiki/Picasso" class="mw-redirect" title="Picasso">Picasso</a> collection matched only by the museums in <a href="/wiki/Museu_Picasso" title="Museu Picasso">Barcelona</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_Picasso" title="Musée Picasso">Paris</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Museum_Schn%C3%BCtgen" class="mw-redirect" title="Museum Schnütgen">Museum Schnütgen</a> of religious art is partly housed in St.&#160;Cecilia, one of Cologne's <a href="/wiki/Twelve_Romanesque_churches_of_Cologne" title="Twelve Romanesque churches of Cologne">Twelve Romanesque churches</a>. Many art galleries in Cologne enjoy an worldwide reputation like e.g. <a href="/wiki/Galerie_Karsten_Greve" title="Galerie Karsten Greve">Galerie Karsten Greve</a>, one of the leading galleries for postwar and contemporary art.</p>
<p>Several orchestras are active in the city, among them the <a href="/wiki/G%C3%BCrzenich_Orchestra" class="mw-redirect" title="Gürzenich Orchestra">Gürzenich Orchestra</a> and the <a href="/wiki/WDR_Symphony_Orchestra_Cologne" title="WDR Symphony Orchestra Cologne">WDR Symphony Orchestra Cologne</a>, both based at the Cologne Philharmonic Orchestra Building.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Other orchestras are the <a href="/wiki/Musica_Antiqua_K%C3%B6ln" title="Musica Antiqua Köln">Musica Antiqua Köln</a> and the <a href="/wiki/WDR_Rundfunkorchester_K%C3%B6ln" title="WDR Rundfunkorchester Köln">WDR Rundfunkorchester Köln</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Cologne_Opera" title="Cologne Opera">Cologne Opera</a> and several choirs, including the <a href="/wiki/WDR_Rundfunkchor_K%C3%B6ln" title="WDR Rundfunkchor Köln">WDR Rundfunkchor Köln</a>. Cologne was also an important hotbed for electronic music in the 1950s (Studio für elektronische Musik, <a href="/wiki/Karlheinz_Stockhausen" title="Karlheinz Stockhausen">Karlheinz Stockhausen</a>) and again from the 1990s onward. The public radio and TV station <a href="/wiki/Westdeutscher_Rundfunk" title="Westdeutscher Rundfunk">WDR</a> was involved in promoting musical movements such as <a href="/wiki/Krautrock" title="Krautrock">Krautrock</a> in the 1970s; the influential <a href="/wiki/Can_(band)" title="Can (band)">Can</a> was formed there in 1968. There are several centres of nightlife, among them the <i>Kwartier Latäng</i> (the student quarter around the Zülpicher Straße) and the nightclub-studded areas around <a href="/wiki/Hohenzollernring" class="mw-redirect" title="Hohenzollernring">Hohenzollernring</a>, Friesenplatz and Rudolfplatz.</p>
<p>The large annual literary festival Lit. Cologne features regional and international authors. The main literary figure connected with Cologne is writer <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_B%C3%B6ll" title="Heinrich Böll">Heinrich Böll</a>, winner of the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_for_Literature" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobel Prize for Literature">Nobel Prize for Literature</a>.</p>
<p>Cologne is well known for its beer, called <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6lsch_(beer)" title="Kölsch (beer)">Kölsch</a>. <a href="/wiki/Colognian_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Colognian language">Kölsch</a> is also the name of the local dialect. This has led to the common joke of Kölsch being the only language one can drink.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cologne_Street_Food_Festival_2017_(32031195374).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Cologne_Street_Food_Festival_2017_%2832031195374%29.jpg/220px-Cologne_Street_Food_Festival_2017_%2832031195374%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Cologne_Street_Food_Festival_2017_%2832031195374%29.jpg/330px-Cologne_Street_Food_Festival_2017_%2832031195374%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Cologne_Street_Food_Festival_2017_%2832031195374%29.jpg/440px-Cologne_Street_Food_Festival_2017_%2832031195374%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4231" data-file-height="2821" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cologne_Street_Food_Festival_2017_(32031195374).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cologne Street Food Festival, 2017</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cologne is also famous for <a href="/wiki/Eau_de_Cologne" title="Eau de Cologne">Eau de Cologne</a> (German: <i>Kölnisch Wasser</i>; lit: "Water of Cologne"), a perfume created by Italian expatriate <a href="/wiki/Johann_Maria_Farina" title="Johann Maria Farina">Johann Maria Farina</a> at the beginning of the 18th century. During the 18th century this perfume became increasingly popular, was exported all over Europe by the Farina family and <i>Farina</i> became a household name for <i>Eau de Cologne</i>. In 1803 Wilhelm Mülhens entered into a contract with an unrelated person from Italy named Carlo Francesco Farina who granted him the right to use his family name and Mühlens opened a small factory at Cologne's Glockengasse. In later years, and after various court battles, his grandson <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_M%C3%BClhens" title="Ferdinand Mülhens">Ferdinand Mülhens</a> was forced to abandon the name <i>Farina</i> for the company and their product. He decided to use the house number given to the factory at Glockengasse during the French occupation in the early 19th century, <a href="/wiki/4711_(brand)" class="mw-redirect" title="4711 (brand)">4711</a>. Today, original Eau de Cologne is still produced in Cologne by both the <a href="/wiki/Johann_Maria_Farina_gegen%C3%BCber_dem_J%C3%BClichs-Platz" title="Johann Maria Farina gegenüber dem Jülichs-Platz">Farina family</a>, currently in the eighth generation, and by <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A4urer_%26_Wirtz" title="Mäurer &amp; Wirtz">Mäurer &amp; Wirtz</a> who bought the 4711 brand in 2006.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Carnival">Carnival</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Carnival">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cologne_carnival" class="mw-redirect" title="Cologne carnival">Cologne carnival</a> is one of the largest street festivals in Europe. In Cologne, the carnival season officially starts on 11 November at 11 minutes past 11&#160;a.m. with the proclamation of the new Carnival Season, and continues until <a href="/wiki/Ash_Wednesday" title="Ash Wednesday">Ash Wednesday</a>. However, the so-called "Tolle Tage" (crazy days) do not start until <i>Weiberfastnacht</i> (Women's Carnival) or, in dialect, <i>Wieverfastelovend</i>, the Thursday before Ash Wednesday, which is the beginning of the street carnival. Zülpicher Strasse and its surroundings, Neumarkt square, Heumarkt and all bars and pubs in the city are crowded with people in costumes dancing and drinking in the streets. Hundreds of thousands of visitors flock to Cologne during this time. Generally, around a million people celebrate in the streets on the Thursday before Ash Wednesday.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Rivalry_with_Düsseldorf"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalry_with_D.C3.BCsseldorf">Rivalry with Düsseldorf</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Rivalry with Düsseldorf">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cologne and <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Düsseldorf">Düsseldorf</a> have a "fierce regional rivalry",<sup id="cite_ref-Rivalry_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rivalry-56">[56]</a></sup> which includes <a href="/wiki/Carnival_in_Germany,_Switzerland_and_Austria" title="Carnival in Germany, Switzerland and Austria">carnival</a> parades, <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>, and beer.<sup id="cite_ref-Rivalry_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rivalry-56">[56]</a></sup> People in Cologne prefer <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6lsch_(beer)" title="Kölsch (beer)">Kölsch</a> while people in Düsseldorf prefer <a href="/wiki/Altbier" title="Altbier">Altbier</a> ("Alt").<sup id="cite_ref-Rivalry_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rivalry-56">[56]</a></sup> Waiters and patrons will "scorn" and make a "mockery" of people who order Alt beer in Cologne or Kölsch in Düsseldorf.<sup id="cite_ref-Rivalry_56-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rivalry-56">[56]</a></sup> The rivalry has been described as a "love–hate relationship".<sup id="cite_ref-Rivalry_56-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rivalry-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Museum_Ludwig_K%C3%B6ln_-_S%C3%BCdeingang_-_Schriftzug.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Museum_Ludwig_K%C3%B6ln_-_S%C3%BCdeingang_-_Schriftzug.jpg/220px-Museum_Ludwig_K%C3%B6ln_-_S%C3%BCdeingang_-_Schriftzug.jpg" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Museum_Ludwig_K%C3%B6ln_-_S%C3%BCdeingang_-_Schriftzug.jpg/330px-Museum_Ludwig_K%C3%B6ln_-_S%C3%BCdeingang_-_Schriftzug.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Museum_Ludwig_K%C3%B6ln_-_S%C3%BCdeingang_-_Schriftzug.jpg/440px-Museum_Ludwig_K%C3%B6ln_-_S%C3%BCdeingang_-_Schriftzug.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1386" /></a>

</div>
<div class="thumb tright">

Roman <a href="/wiki/Excavation_(archaeology)" title="Excavation (archaeology)">excavation</a> in Cologne: <a href="/wiki/Dionysus" title="Dionysus">Dionysus</a> Mosaic on display at <a href="/wiki/R%C3%B6misch-Germanisches_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="Römisch-Germanisches Museum">Römisch-Germanisches Museum</a></div>
</div>

<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_museums_in_Cologne" title="List of museums in Cologne">List of museums in Cologne</a></div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fragrance_Museum" title="Fragrance Museum">Farina Fragrance Museum</a> – birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Eau_de_Cologne" title="Eau de Cologne">Eau de Cologne</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/R%C3%B6misch-Germanisches_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="Römisch-Germanisches Museum">Römisch-Germanisches Museum</a> (Roman-Germanic Museum) – ancient Roman and Germanic culture</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wallraf-Richartz_Museum" title="Wallraf-Richartz Museum">Wallraf-Richartz Museum</a> – European painting from the 13th to the early 20th century</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Museum_Ludwig" title="Museum Ludwig">Museum Ludwig</a> – modern art</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Museum_Schn%C3%BCtgen" class="mw-redirect" title="Museum Schnütgen">Museum Schnütgen</a> – medieval art</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Museum_f%C3%BCr_Angewandte_Kunst_(Cologne)" title="Museum für Angewandte Kunst (Cologne)">Museum für Angewandte Kunst</a> – <a href="/wiki/Applied_art" class="mw-redirect" title="Applied art">applied art</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kolumba" title="Kolumba">Kolumba Kunstmuseum des Erzbistums Köln</a> (<a href="/wiki/Art_museum" title="Art museum">art museum</a> of the Archbishopric of Cologne) – modern art museum built around medieval ruins, completed 2007</li>
<li>Cathedral Treasury "Domschatzkammer" – historic underground vaults of the Cathedral</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/EL-DE_Haus" title="EL-DE Haus">EL-DE Haus</a> – former local headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Gestapo" title="Gestapo">Gestapo</a> houses a museum documenting <a href="/wiki/Nazi" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi">Nazi</a> rule in Cologne with a special focus on the persecution of political dissenters and minorities</li>
<li>German Sports and Olympic Museum – exhibitions about sports from antiquity until the present</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Imhoff-Schokoladenmuseum" title="Imhoff-Schokoladenmuseum">Imhoff-Schokoladenmuseum</a> – Chocolate Museum</li>
<li>Geomuseum of the University of Cologne - the exhibition includes fossils (such as <a href="/wiki/Dinosaur" title="Dinosaur">dinosaur</a> bones and the skeleton of an <a href="/wiki/Eryops" title="Eryops">Eryops</a>), <a href="/wiki/Stones" class="mw-redirect" title="Stones">stones</a> and <a href="/wiki/Minerals" class="mw-redirect" title="Minerals">minerals</a></li>
<li>Forum for Internet Technology in Contemporary Art – collections of Internet-based art, corporate part of (NewMediaArtProjectNetwork):cologne, the experimental platform for art and New Media</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Flora_und_Botanischer_Garten_K%C3%B6ln" title="Flora und Botanischer Garten Köln">Flora und Botanischer Garten Köln</a> - the city's formal park and main <a href="/wiki/Botanical_garden" title="Botanical garden">botanical garden</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Forstbotanischer_Garten_K%C3%B6ln" title="Forstbotanischer Garten Köln">Forstbotanischer Garten Köln</a> - an <a href="/wiki/Arboretum" title="Arboretum">arboretum</a> and woodland <a href="/wiki/Botanical_garden" title="Botanical garden">botanical garden</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_fairs_and_festivals">Music fairs and festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Music fairs and festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city was home to the internationally famous <a href="/wiki/Ringfest" title="Ringfest">Ringfest</a>, and now to the C/o pop festival.<sup id="cite_ref-C.2Fo_pop_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C.2Fo_pop-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition, Cologne enjoys a thriving Christmas Market Weihnachtsmarkt presence with several locations in the city.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Koelnmesse_Nordeingang.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Koelnmesse_Nordeingang.jpg/220px-Koelnmesse_Nordeingang.jpg" width="220" height="66" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Koelnmesse_Nordeingang.jpg/330px-Koelnmesse_Nordeingang.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Koelnmesse_Nordeingang.jpg/440px-Koelnmesse_Nordeingang.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="1800" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Koelnmesse_Nordeingang.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
North entrance to <a href="/wiki/Koelnmesse" title="Koelnmesse">Koelnmesse</a>, 2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rheinauhafen_-_The_Bench_-_Rheinseite_(1828-30).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Rheinauhafen_-_The_Bench_-_Rheinseite_%281828-30%29.jpg/220px-Rheinauhafen_-_The_Bench_-_Rheinseite_%281828-30%29.jpg" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Rheinauhafen_-_The_Bench_-_Rheinseite_%281828-30%29.jpg/330px-Rheinauhafen_-_The_Bench_-_Rheinseite_%281828-30%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Rheinauhafen_-_The_Bench_-_Rheinseite_%281828-30%29.jpg/440px-Rheinauhafen_-_The_Bench_-_Rheinseite_%281828-30%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3300" data-file-height="2100" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rheinauhafen_-_The_Bench_-_Rheinseite_(1828-30).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Modern office building at <a href="/wiki/Rheinauhafen" title="Rheinauhafen">Rheinauhafen</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As the largest city in the <a href="/wiki/Rhine-Ruhr" title="Rhine-Ruhr">Rhine-Ruhr</a> metropolitan region, Cologne benefits from a large <a href="/wiki/Market_structure" title="Market structure">market structure</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> In competition with <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Düsseldorf">Düsseldorf</a>, the economy of Cologne is primarily based on <a href="/wiki/Insurance_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Insurance industry">insurance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Media_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Media industry">media industries</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> while the city is also an important cultural and research centre and home to a number of <a href="/wiki/Corporate_headquarters" title="Corporate headquarters">corporate headquarters</a>.</p>
<p>Among the largest media companies based in Cologne are <a href="/wiki/Westdeutscher_Rundfunk" title="Westdeutscher Rundfunk">Westdeutscher Rundfunk</a>, <a href="/wiki/RTL_Television" title="RTL Television">RTL Television</a> (with subsidiaries), <a href="/wiki/N-tv" title="N-tv">n-tv</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deutschlandradio" title="Deutschlandradio">Deutschlandradio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brainpool_TV" title="Brainpool TV">Brainpool TV</a> and publishing houses like J.&#160;P. Bachem, <a href="/wiki/Taschen" title="Taschen">Taschen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tandem_Verlag" title="Tandem Verlag">Tandem Verlag</a>, and <a href="/wiki/M._DuMont_Schauberg" title="M. DuMont Schauberg">M.&#160;DuMont Schauberg</a>. Several clusters of media, arts and communications agencies, TV production studios, and state agencies work partly with private and government-funded cultural institutions. Among the insurance companies based in Cologne are Central, DEVK, DKV, <a href="/wiki/Generali_Deutschland" title="Generali Deutschland">Generali Deutschland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gen_Re" title="Gen Re">Gen Re</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gothaer_Group" title="Gothaer Group">Gothaer</a>, HDI Gerling and national headquarters of <a href="/wiki/AXA" title="AXA">AXA</a> Insurance, Mitsui Sumitomo Insurance Group and <a href="/wiki/Zurich_Financial_Services" class="mw-redirect" title="Zurich Financial Services">Zurich Financial Services</a>.</p>
<p>The German flag carrier <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a> and its subsidiary <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_CityLine" title="Lufthansa CityLine">Lufthansa CityLine</a> have their main corporate headquarters in Cologne.<sup id="cite_ref-FI_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FI-60">[60]</a></sup> The largest employer in Cologne is <a href="/wiki/Ford_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Europe">Ford Europe</a>, which has its European headquarters and a factory in Niehl (<a href="/wiki/Ford_Germany" title="Ford Germany">Ford-Werke GmbH</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Motorsport_GmbH" title="Toyota Motorsport GmbH">Toyota Motorsport GmbH</a> (TMG), <a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota</a>'s official motorsports team, responsible for Toyota rally cars, and then <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> cars, has its headquarters and workshops in Cologne. Other large companies based in Cologne include the <a href="/wiki/REWE_Group" title="REWE Group">REWE Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/T%C3%9CV_Rheinland" class="mw-redirect" title="TÜV Rheinland">TÜV Rheinland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deutz_AG" title="Deutz AG">Deutz AG</a> and a number of <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6lsch_(beer)" title="Kölsch (beer)">Kölsch</a> breweries. Cologne has the country's highest density of pubs per capita.<sup id="cite_ref-Nightlife_50-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nightlife-50">[50]</a></sup> The largest three Kölsch breweries are Reissdorf, Gaffel, and Früh.</p>

<p>Historically, Cologne has always been an important trade city, with land, air, and sea connections.<sup id="cite_ref-Cologneeconomy_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cologneeconomy-2">[2]</a></sup> The city has five Rhine ports,<sup id="cite_ref-Cologneeconomy_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cologneeconomy-2">[2]</a></sup> the second largest <a href="/wiki/Inland_port" title="Inland port">inland port</a> in Germany and one of the largest in Europe. <a href="/wiki/Cologne-Bonn_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Cologne-Bonn Airport">Cologne-Bonn Airport</a> is the second largest freight terminal in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-Cologneeconomy_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cologneeconomy-2">[2]</a></sup> Today, the <a href="/wiki/Cologne_trade_fair" class="mw-redirect" title="Cologne trade fair">Cologne trade fair</a> (<i>Koelnmesse</i>) ranks as a major European trade fair location with over 50 trade fairs<sup id="cite_ref-Cologneeconomy_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cologneeconomy-2">[2]</a></sup> and other large cultural and sports events. In 2008 Cologne had 4.31&#160;million overnight stays booked and 2.38&#160;million arrivals.<sup id="cite_ref-Cologneglance_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cologneglance-25">[25]</a></sup> Cologne's largest daily newspaper is the <i><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6lner_Stadt-Anzeiger" title="Kölner Stadt-Anzeiger">Kölner Stadt-Anzeiger</a></i>.</p>
<p>Cologne shows a significant increase in <a href="/wiki/Startup_companies" class="mw-redirect" title="Startup companies">startup companies</a>, especially when considering digital business.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Cologne" title="Transport in Cologne">Transport in Cologne</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road_transport">Road transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Road transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Koelner_Ring.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Koelner_Ring.png/220px-Koelner_Ring.png" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Koelner_Ring.png/330px-Koelner_Ring.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Koelner_Ring.png/440px-Koelner_Ring.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Koelner_Ring.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Major <a href="/wiki/List_of_streets_in_Cologne" title="List of streets in Cologne">roads through and around Cologne</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Road building had been a major issue in the 1920s under the leadership of mayor <a href="/wiki/Konrad_Adenauer" title="Konrad Adenauer">Konrad Adenauer</a>. The first German limited access road was constructed after 1929 between Cologne and <a href="/wiki/Bonn" title="Bonn">Bonn</a>. Today, this is the <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_555" title="Bundesautobahn 555">Bundesautobahn 555</a>. In 1965, Cologne became the first German city to be fully encircled by a motorway ringroad. Roughly at the same time a city centre bypass (<i>Stadtautobahn</i>) was planned, but only partially put into effect, due to opposition by environmental groups. The completed section became <i>Bundesstraße ("Federal Road") B 55a</i>, which begins at the <i>Zoobrücke</i> ("Zoo Bridge") and meets with <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_4" title="Bundesautobahn 4">A&#160;4</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_3" title="Bundesautobahn 3">A&#160;3</a> at the interchange Cologne East. Nevertheless, it is referred to as <i>Stadtautobahn</i> by most locals. In contrast to this the <i>Nord-Süd-Fahrt</i> ("North-South-Drive") was actually completed, a new four/six-lane city centre through-route, which had already been anticipated by planners such as <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Schumacher_(architect)" title="Fritz Schumacher (architect)">Fritz Schumacher</a> in the 1920s. The last section south of <i>Ebertplatz</i> was completed in 1972.</p>
<p>In 2005, the first stretch of an eight-lane motorway in <a href="/wiki/North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="North Rhine-Westphalia">North Rhine-Westphalia</a> was opened to traffic on <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_3" title="Bundesautobahn 3">Bundesautobahn&#160;3</a>, part of the eastern section of the <a href="/wiki/Cologne_Beltway" title="Cologne Beltway">Cologne Beltway</a> between the interchanges Cologne East and Heumar.</p>

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:146_019-5_Rheinexpressinkoelnhbf.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Train at <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ln_Hauptbahnhof" title="Köln Hauptbahnhof">Köln Hauptbahnhof</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Compared to other German cities, Cologne has a traffic layout that is not very <a href="/wiki/Bicycle-friendly" title="Bicycle-friendly">bicycle-friendly</a>. It has repeatedly ranked among the worst in an independent evaluation<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> conducted by the <a href="/wiki/Allgemeiner_Deutscher_Fahrrad-Club" title="Allgemeiner Deutscher Fahrrad-Club">Allgemeiner Deutscher Fahrrad-Club</a>. In 2014 it ranked 36th out of 39 German cities with a population greater than 200,000.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail_transport">Rail transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Rail transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cologne has a railway service with <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bahn" title="Deutsche Bahn">Deutsche Bahn</a> <a href="/wiki/InterCity" title="InterCity">InterCity</a> and <a href="/wiki/InterCityExpress" class="mw-redirect" title="InterCityExpress">ICE</a>-trains stopping at <i><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ln_Hauptbahnhof" title="Köln Hauptbahnhof">Köln Hauptbahnhof</a></i> (Cologne Main Station), <i><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ln_Messe/Deutz_station" title="Köln Messe/Deutz station">Köln Messe/Deutz</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Cologne/Bonn_Airport_station" title="Cologne/Bonn Airport station">Cologne/Bonn Airport</a></i>. ICE and <a href="/wiki/Thalys" title="Thalys">TGV Thalys</a> high-speed trains link Cologne with <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, Brussels (in 1h47, 9 departures/day) and Paris (in 3h14, 6 departures/day). There are frequent ICE trains to other German cities, including <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_am_Main" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt am Main">Frankfurt am Main</a> and Berlin. ICE Trains to London via the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Tunnel" title="Channel Tunnel">Channel Tunnel</a> were planned for 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cologne_Stadtbahn" title="Cologne Stadtbahn">Cologne Stadtbahn</a> operated by <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6lner_Verkehrs-Betriebe" class="mw-redirect" title="Kölner Verkehrs-Betriebe">Kölner Verkehrsbetriebe</a> (KVB)<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> is an <a href="/wiki/List_of_Cologne_KVB_stations" title="List of Cologne KVB stations">extensive</a> <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">light rail</a> system that is partially underground and serves Cologne and a number of neighbouring cities. It evolved from the <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">tram</a> system. Nearby <a href="/wiki/Bonn" title="Bonn">Bonn</a> is linked by both the Stadtbahn and main line railway trains, and occasional recreational boats on the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a>. <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Düsseldorf">Düsseldorf</a> is also linked by <a href="/wiki/S-Bahn" class="mw-redirect" title="S-Bahn">S-Bahn</a> trains, which are operated by Deutsche Bahn.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Rhine-Ruhr_S-Bahn" title="Rhine-Ruhr S-Bahn">Rhine-Ruhr S-Bahn</a> has 5 lines which cross Cologne.The S13/S19 runs 24/7 between Cologne Hbf and Cologne/Bonn airport.</p>
<p>There are also frequent buses covering most of the city and surrounding suburbs, and <a href="/wiki/Eurolines" title="Eurolines">Eurolines</a> coaches to London via <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_transport">Water transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Water transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/H%C3%A4fen_und_G%C3%BCterverkehr_K%C3%B6ln" class="mw-redirect" title="Häfen und Güterverkehr Köln">Häfen und Güterverkehr Köln</a></i> (Ports and Goods traffic Cologne, HGK) is one of the largest operators of <a href="/wiki/Inland_port" title="Inland port">inland ports</a> in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Ports include Köln-Deutz, Köln-Godorf, and Köln-Niehl&#160;I and II.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_transport">Air transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Air transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cologne's international airport is <a href="/wiki/Cologne_Bonn_Airport" title="Cologne Bonn Airport">Cologne/Bonn Airport</a> (CGN). It is also called Konrad Adenauer Airport after Germany's first post-war Chancellor <a href="/wiki/Konrad_Adenauer" title="Konrad Adenauer">Konrad Adenauer</a>, who was born in the city and was <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Cologne" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayor of Cologne">mayor of Cologne</a> from 1917 until 1933. The airport is shared with the neighbouring city of <a href="/wiki/Bonn" title="Bonn">Bonn</a>. Cologne is headquarters to the <a href="/wiki/European_Aviation_Safety_Agency" title="European Aviation Safety Agency">European Aviation Safety Agency</a> (EASA). The airport is also the main hub of the airline <a href="/wiki/Germanwings" title="Germanwings">Germanwings</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Cologne is home to numerous universities and colleges,<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> and host to some 72,000 students.<sup id="cite_ref-Cologneeconomy_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cologneeconomy-2">[2]</a></sup> Its oldest university, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cologne" title="University of Cologne">University of Cologne</a> (founded in 1388<sup id="cite_ref-Cologne_History_3-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cologne_History-3">[3]</a></sup>) is the largest university in Germany, as the <a href="/wiki/Cologne_University_of_Applied_Sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="Cologne University of Applied Sciences">Cologne University of Applied Sciences</a> is the largest <a href="/wiki/Fachhochschule" title="Fachhochschule">university of Applied Sciences</a> in the country. The Cologne University of Music and Dance is the largest <a href="/wiki/Music_school" title="Music school">conservatory</a> in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Foreigners can have German lessons in the VHS (Adult Education Centre).<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Within Germany, Cologne is known as an important media centre. Several radio and television stations, including <a href="/wiki/Westdeutscher_Rundfunk" title="Westdeutscher Rundfunk">Westdeutscher Rundfunk</a> (WDR), <a href="/wiki/RTL_Television" title="RTL Television">RTL</a> and <a href="/wiki/VOX_(TV_channel)" title="VOX (TV channel)">VOX</a>, have their headquarters in the city. Film and TV production is also important. The city is "Germany's capital of TV crime stories".<sup id="cite_ref-CologneProduction_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CologneProduction-71">[71]</a></sup> A third of all German TV productions are made in the <a href="/wiki/Cologne_(region)" title="Cologne (region)">Cologne region</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CologneProduction_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CologneProduction-71">[71]</a></sup> Furthermore, the city hosts the <a href="/wiki/Cologne_Comedy_Festival" title="Cologne Comedy Festival">Cologne Comedy Festival</a>, which is considered to be the largest comedy festival in mainland Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FIFA_WM06_Stadion_Koeln.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/FIFA_WM06_Stadion_Koeln.jpg/230px-FIFA_WM06_Stadion_Koeln.jpg" width="230" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/FIFA_WM06_Stadion_Koeln.jpg/345px-FIFA_WM06_Stadion_Koeln.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/FIFA_WM06_Stadion_Koeln.jpg/460px-FIFA_WM06_Stadion_Koeln.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FIFA_WM06_Stadion_Koeln.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/RheinEnergieStadion" title="RheinEnergieStadion">RheinEnergieStadion</a> is the stadium of <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> club <a href="/wiki/1._FC_K%C3%B6ln" title="1. FC Köln">1. FC Köln</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cologne hosts <a href="/wiki/1._FC_K%C3%B6ln" title="1. FC Köln">1. FC Köln</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Colognesports_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colognesports-73">[73]</a></sup> who play in the <a href="/wiki/1._Bundesliga" class="mw-redirect" title="1. Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a>. They play their home matches in <a href="/wiki/RheinEnergieStadion" title="RheinEnergieStadion">RheinEnergieStadion</a> which also hosted 5 matches of the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 FIFA World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-K.C3.B6lnstadion_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-K.C3.B6lnstadion-74">[74]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">International Olympic Committee</a> and Internationale Vereinigung Sport- und Freizeiteinrichtungen e.V. gave RheinEnergieStadion a bronze medal for "being one of the best sporting venues in the world".<sup id="cite_ref-K.C3.B6lnstadion_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-K.C3.B6lnstadion-74">[74]</a></sup> Cologne also hosts <a href="/wiki/FC_Viktoria_K%C3%B6ln_1904" class="mw-redirect" title="FC Viktoria Köln 1904">FC Viktoria Köln 1904</a> and <a href="/wiki/SC_Fortuna_K%C3%B6ln" title="SC Fortuna Köln">SC Fortuna Köln</a>, who play in the <a href="/wiki/Fu%C3%9Fball-Regionalliga_West" class="mw-redirect" title="Fußball-Regionalliga West">Regionalliga West</a> (fourth division) respectively the <a href="/wiki/3._Liga" title="3. Liga">3. Liga</a> (third division).</p>
<p>The city is also home of the ice hockey team <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6lner_Haie" title="Kölner Haie">Kölner Haie</a>, in the highest <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> league in Germany, the <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Eishockey_Liga" title="Deutsche Eishockey Liga">Deutsche Eishockey Liga</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Colognesports_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colognesports-73">[73]</a></sup> They are based at <a href="/wiki/Lanxess_Arena" title="Lanxess Arena">Lanxess Arena</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Colognesports_73-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colognesports-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>Several horse races per year are held at <a href="/wiki/Cologne-Weidenpesch_Racecourse" title="Cologne-Weidenpesch Racecourse">Cologne-Weidenpesch Racecourse</a> since 1897, the annual <a href="/wiki/Cologne_Marathon" title="Cologne Marathon">Cologne Marathon</a> was started in 1997. From 2002 to 2009, the Panasonic <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Racing" title="Toyota Racing">Toyota Racing</a> <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> team was based in the Marsdorf suburb, at the <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Motorsport_GmbH" title="Toyota Motorsport GmbH">Toyota Motorsport GmbH</a> facility.</p>
<p>Cologne is considered "the secret golf capital of Germany".<sup id="cite_ref-Colognesports_73-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colognesports-73">[73]</a></sup> The first golf club in <a href="/wiki/North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="North Rhine-Westphalia">North Rhine-Westphalia</a> was founded in Cologne in 1906.<sup id="cite_ref-Colognesports_73-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colognesports-73">[73]</a></sup> The city offers the most options and top events in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-Colognesports_73-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colognesports-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city has hosted several athletic events which includes the <a href="/wiki/2005_FIFA_Confederations_Cup" title="2005 FIFA Confederations Cup">2005 FIFA Confederations Cup</a>, 2006 FIFA World Cup, <a href="/wiki/2007_World_Men%27s_Handball_Championship" title="2007 World Men's Handball Championship">2007 World Men's Handball Championship</a>, <a href="/wiki/2010_IIHF_World_Championship" title="2010 IIHF World Championship">2010</a> and <a href="/wiki/2017_IIHF_World_Championship" title="2017 IIHF World Championship">2017 Ice Hockey World Championships</a> and <a href="/wiki/2010_Gay_Games" title="2010 Gay Games">2010 Gay Games</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Facts_and_figures_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Facts_and_figures-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_residents">Notable residents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Notable residents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Notable people, whose roots can be found in Cologne:</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Konrad_Adenauer" title="Konrad Adenauer">Konrad Adenauer</a> (1876–1967), politician, mayor of Cologne (1917–33, 1945) and first <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_Germany_(Federal_Republic)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chancellor of Germany (Federal Republic)">West German Federal Chancellor</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Cornelius_Agrippa" title="Heinrich Cornelius Agrippa">Heinrich Cornelius Agrippa</a> (1486–1535), alchemist, <a href="/wiki/Occult" title="Occult">occultist</a>, and author of <i><a href="/wiki/De_occulta_philosophia_libri_tres" class="mw-redirect" title="De occulta philosophia libri tres">Three Books of Occult Philosophy</a></i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Agrippina_the_Younger" title="Agrippina the Younger">Agrippina the Younger</a> (15–59), Roman Empress (wife of Emperor <a href="/wiki/Claudius" title="Claudius">Claudius</a>) and mother of Emperor <a href="/wiki/Nero" title="Nero">Nero</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Birnbaum" title="Heinrich Birnbaum">Heinrich Birnbaum</a> (1403–73), a Catholic monk</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Boigk" class="mw-redirect" title="Heinrich Boigk">Heinrich Boigk</a> (1912–2003), <a href="/wiki/Knight%27s_Cross_of_the_Iron_Cross" title="Knight's Cross of the Iron Cross">Knights Cross</a> winner</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_Blum" title="Robert Blum">Robert Blum</a> (1807–48), German politician and martyr of the 19th century democratic movement in Germany</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Heinrich_B%C3%B6ll" title="Heinrich Böll">Heinrich Böll</a> (1917–85), German writer and winner of the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_prize_for_literature" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobel prize for literature">Nobel prize for literature</a> in 1972</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Georg_Braun" title="Georg Braun">Georg Braun</a> (1541-1622), topogeographer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Max_Bruch" title="Max Bruch">Max Bruch</a> (1838–1920), composer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/%C3%81lex_Calatrava" title="Álex Calatrava">Álex Calatrava</a> (born 1973), Spanish professional tennis player</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Heribert_Calleen" title="Heribert Calleen">Heribert Calleen</a> (born 1924), German sculptor</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Florian_Henckel_von_Donnersmarck" title="Florian Henckel von Donnersmarck">Florian Henckel von Donnersmarck</a> (born 1973), <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a>-winning director and screenwriter</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Max_Ernst" title="Max Ernst">Max Ernst</a> (1891–1976), German painter and artist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kota_Ezawa" title="Kota Ezawa">Kota Ezawa</a> (born 1969), Japanese German animator and artist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Angela_Gossow" title="Angela Gossow">Angela Gossow</a> (born 1974), former German lead vocalist of Swedish melodic death metal band <a href="/wiki/Arch_Enemy" title="Arch Enemy">Arch Enemy</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Everhard_von_Groote&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Everhard von Groote (page does not exist)">Everhard von Groote</a> (1798–1864), Germanist and writer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Britta_Heidemann" title="Britta Heidemann">Britta Heidemann</a> (born 1982), <a href="/wiki/%C3%89p%C3%A9e" title="Épée">épée</a> fencer and <a href="/wiki/Olympic_medalist" class="mw-redirect" title="Olympic medalist">Olympic medalist</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/H._Robert_Heller" title="H. Robert Heller">H. Robert Heller</a> (born 1940), former professor, Governor of the Federal Reserve System and President of VISA U.S.A.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Trude_Herr" title="Trude Herr">Trude Herr</a> (1927–91), actress and singer</li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_Relations">International Relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: International Relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Germany" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in Germany">List of twin towns and sister cities in Germany</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_and_sister_cities">Twin towns and sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cologne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Twin towns and sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cologne is <a href="/wiki/Twin_towns_and_sister_cities" class="mw-redirect" title="Twin towns and sister cities">twinned</a> with:</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, Spain (since 1984)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Berlin-Neuk%C3%B6lln" class="mw-redirect" title="Berlin-Neukölln">Berlin-Neukölln</a>, Germany</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Berlin-Treptow" class="mw-redirect" title="Berlin-Treptow">Berlin-Treptow</a>, Germany</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bethlehem" title="Bethlehem">Bethlehem</a>, Palestine (1996)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cluj_Napoca" class="mw-redirect" title="Cluj Napoca">Cluj Napoca</a>/Klausenburg, Romania (1976)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Corinto,_Nicaragua" title="Corinto, Nicaragua">Corinto</a>/El Realejo, Nicaragua (1988)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cork_(city)" title="Cork (city)">Cork</a>, Ireland (27. June 1988)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Esch-sur-Alzette" title="Esch-sur-Alzette">Esch-sur-Alzette</a>, Luxembourg (1958)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Indianapolis" title="Indianapolis">Indianapolis</a>, USA</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>, Turkey (1997)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Katowice" title="Katowice">Katowice</a>, Poland (15. March, 1991)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kyoto" title="Kyoto">Kyoto</a>, Japan (21. January, 1963)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lille" title="Lille">Lille</a>, France (1958)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a>, UK (1952)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/L%C3%BCttich" class="mw-redirect" title="Lüttich">Lüttich</a>, Belgium (1958)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>, China (14. September, 1987)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>, Brasil (19. September, 2011)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a>, Netherlands (1958)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv-Yafo" class="mw-redirect" title="Tel Aviv-Yafo">Tel Aviv-Yafo</a>, Israel (6. August, 1979)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a>, Greece (3. May, 1988)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tunis" title="Tunis">Tunis</a>, Tunisia (12. June, 1964)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Turin" title="Turin">Turin</a>, Italy (1958)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Turku" title="Turku">Turku</a>, Finland (1967)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Volgograd" title="Volgograd">Volgograd</a>, Russia</li>
</ul>
</div>

<td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="3" style="padding:0.2em 0.4em 0.4em;line-height:1.25em;">
<div>
<div class="plainlist">
<ul>
<li><sup><small>1</small></sup> <a class="mw-selflink selflink">Cologne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dortmund" title="Dortmund">Dortmund</a> were both capital of the Westphalian Quarter at different times.</li>
<li><sup><small>2</small></sup> <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a> gained importance once <a href="/wiki/Bruges" title="Bruges">Bruges</a> became inaccessible due to the silting of the <a href="/wiki/Zwin" title="Zwin">Zwin</a> channel.</li>
</ul>
</div>
</div>
